{"Quotes": "", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using a combination of surface science techniques and density functional theory (DFT) modeling. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research. The unique surface activity on the bimetallic systems is observed only when annealed to 600 K. Deposition of a monolayer coverage of Ni on Pt(111) at 300 K produces reactivity similar to those on Ni surfaces. On the other hand, after heating the surfaces to 600 K, probe reactions show surface activity unlike those on Ni, Co, or Pt(111) surfaces. Additional experimental characterization and theoretical studies determined that the differences between the 300 and 600 K bimetallic surfaces were due to diffusion of monolayer Ni into the subsurface region of Pt(111), producing the PtNiPt(111) surface structures.", "Chinese": "通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层来合成Ni/Pt双金属表面，其表征结合了表面科学技术和密度泛函理论（DFT）建模。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要，这些表面在先进的表面科学和催化研究的背景下。在将双金属系统退火至600 K时，观察到独特的表面活性。在300 K下在Pt(111)上沉积单层Ni覆盖层产生的反应性与Ni表面上的反应性相似。另一方面，在将表面加热至600 K后，探针反应显示出与Ni、Co或Pt(111)表面上的反应性不同的表面活性。额外的实验表征和理论研究确定，300 K和600 K双金属表面之间的差异是由于单层Ni扩散到Pt(111)的次表面区域，产生了PtNiPt(111)表面结构。", "Doi": "10.1021/jp061697z"},
{"Quotes": "", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is not explicitly described in the literature. However, the process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research because it allows for the investigation of the influence of structural parameters on catalytic activity and magnetism of an alloy. The NiPt system is an interesting candidate for investigations due to its high catalytic selectivity for certain reactions and the strong interplay between magnetic and spatial order. It also allows for the investigation of atomic scale interactions and the formation of metastable alloy phases. The study shows that Ni atoms exchange with Pt at both terrace and step sites, forming a one-dimensional ordered alloy at the step edges and randomly embedding in Pt on the terraces. At higher temperatures, a 2x2 substitutional alloy is formed, corresponding to a Ni20Pt80 composition of the surface topmost layer. This detailed characterization is essential for modeling and computational studies, providing insights into the structural and electronic properties of Ni/Pt surfaces, which are critical for catalysis and other surface science applications.", "Chinese": "在文献中没有明确描述通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基板上沉积Ni单层来合成Ni/Pt双金属表面的表征过程。然而，这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要，特别是在高级表面科学和催化研究的背景下，因为它允许研究结构参数对合金催化活性和磁性的影响。NiPt系统是研究的有趣候选者，因为它对某些反应具有高催化选择性，并且在磁性和空间秩序之间存在强烈的相互作用。它还允许研究原子尺度的相互作用和亚稳合金相的形成。研究表明，Ni原子在台阶和台地位置与Pt交换，在台阶边缘形成一维有序合金，在台地上随机嵌入Pt。在较高温度下，形成了2x2置换合金，对应于表面顶层Ni20Pt80的组成。这种详细的表征对于建模和计算研究至关重要，为Ni/Pt表面的结构和电子性质提供了见解，这对于催化和其他表面科学应用至关重要。", "Doi": "10.1016/s0039-6028(01)00696-3"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"The characterization of Ni/Pt(111) bimetallic surfaces is very useful in providing structural models for DFT calculations.\"\n          [2] \"It is also critical in correlating bimetallic structures with the electronic and chemical properties of bimetallic surfaces.\"\n          [3] \"The AES, LEIS, XPS, and STM results confirmed the presence of a surface Ni monolayer on Pt(111) after the deposition of Ni at 300 K.\"\n          [4] \"The characterization following annealing to 600640 K was consistent with the diffusion of Ni into the subsurface region of Pt(111); the possibility of the production of the PtNiPt(111) structure, with Ni atoms staying directly underneath the surface Pt, was further suggested from DFT calculations and experimental measurements of chemical properties.\"", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using various techniques such as Low Energy Ion Scattering (LEIS), Auger Electron Spectroscopy (AES), X-ray Photoelectron Spectroscopy (XPS), and Scanning Tunneling Microscopy (STM). This process is crucial for structural modeling and Density Functional Theory (DFT) calculations as it provides detailed information about the surface structure. Additionally, it is critical for understanding the correlation between bimetallic structures and their electronic and chemical properties, which is essential for advanced surface science and catalysis research. The AES, LEIS, XPS, and STM results confirmed the presence of a surface Ni monolayer on Pt(111) after the deposition of Ni at 300 K. After annealing to 600-640 K, the characterization was consistent with the diffusion of Ni into the subsurface region of Pt(111), suggesting the production of the PtNiPt(111) structure, with Ni atoms staying directly underneath the surface Pt. This process is essential for advanced surface science and catalysis research.", "Chinese": "通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层来合成Ni/Pt双金属表面，其表征采用低能离子散射（LEIS）、俄歇电子能谱（AES）、X射线光电子能谱（XPS）和扫描隧道显微镜（STM）等多种技术进行。这一过程对于结构建模和密度泛函理论（DFT）计算至关重要，因为它提供了关于表面结构的详细信息。此外，对于理解双金属结构与其电子和化学性质之间的关联，这对于先进的表面科学和催化研究是至关重要的。AES、LEIS、XPS和STM结果证实，在300 K下沉积Ni后，Pt(111)上存在表面Ni单层。在600-640 K下退火后，表征结果与Ni扩散到Pt(111)的次表面区域一致，表明可能产生PtNiPt(111)结构，Ni原子直接位于表面Pt下方。这一过程对于先进的表面科学和催化研究至关重要。", "Doi": "10.1021/cr300096b_2"},

{"Quotes": "", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using low-energy electron diffraction (LEED) and Auger electron spectroscopy (AES). This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research because it allows us to observe the initial growth and the alloy formation of Ni ultrathin films on Pt(111) surface. Several interesting structural phases were observed in this system: pseudo-(1×1), coherent epitaxy, incoherent epitaxy, and (2×2). The phase diagram was determined by LEED. In addition, the formation of NiPt alloy was investigated at various Ni coverages. The starting temperature for the alloy formation increases significantly as the Ni thin films turn into three-dimensional islands. This process can also provide insights into their magnetic properties and catalytic activities.", "Chinese": "通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基板上沉积Ni单层来合成Ni/Pt双金属表面的表征是通过使用低能电子衍射(LEED)和Auger电子光谱(AES)进行的。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解在高级表面科学和催化研究的背景下至关重要，因为它使我们能够观察Ni超薄膜在Pt(111)表面的初始生长和合金形成。在这个系统中观察到了几种有趣的结构相:伪-(1×1),相干外延,非相干外延和(2×2)。相图由LEED确定。此外,在不同的Ni覆盖度下研究了NiPt合金的形成。随着Ni薄膜变成三维岛屿，合金形成的起始温度显著增加。这一过程还可以为它们的磁性和催化活性提供见解。", "Doi": "10.1016/s0039-6028(01)02022-2"},

{"Quotes": "", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted through a combination of experimental techniques and theoretical calculations. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research because it allows for the validation of theoretical predictions with experimental data. By comparing the results from DFT modeling with surface science experiments, researchers can gain insights into the unique chemical properties of bimetallic surfaces, such as the Ni/Pt system, which displays novel catalytic behavior due to the interaction between the subsurface Ni and the surface Pt atoms. This interaction leads to a shift in the d-band center of the surface Pt atoms, resulting in a reduction in the adsorption energy of hydrogen and olefins compared to pure Pt or Ni surfaces. The combination of DFT and experimental techniques provides a powerful tool for the rational design of bimetallic catalysts with improved activity and selectivity for various chemical reactions, including the low-temperature hydrogenation of olefins. The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research. This process allows us to determine the precise atomic structure of the bimetallic surfaces, which is essential for accurate DFT calculations. The structural information obtained through characterization techniques such as Auger electron spectroscopy (AES), temperature-programmed desorption (TPD), and high-resolution electron energy loss spectroscopy (HREELS) provides the necessary input for DFT modeling. This modeling, in turn, helps us understand the electronic properties of the surfaces, such as the d-band center, which is crucial for predicting the adsorption energies of molecules like hydrogen and ethylene. The combination of experimental characterization and theoretical calculations enables a deeper understanding of the catalytic properties of bimetallic surfaces, facilitating the rational design of catalysts with improved activity and selectivity. When Ni is deposited with the Pt(111) surface held at 300 K, Ni atoms stay on the topmost layer to produce the NiPt(111) surface MBS structure. If this surface is subsequently heated to 600 K, or if the monolayer deposition occurs with the Pt(111) substrate held at 600 K, most of the Ni atoms diffuse into the subsurface region to produce the PtNiPt(111) subsurface MBS structure. The surfaces are characterized using AES, XPS, LEIS, and STM. The LEIS and AES results following the annealing of the 300 K NiPt(111) surface to 900 K are shown in Fig. 5. The normal and grazing emission XPS of the NiPt(111) surface prepared at 300 K and the PtNiPt(111) subsurface structure prepared at 600 K are shown in Fig. 6. STM was also utilized to further characterize the morphology of the 300 K and 600 K surfaces. The AES, LEIS, XPS, and STM results confirmed the presence of a surface Ni monolayer on Pt(111) after the deposition of Ni at 300 K. The characterization following the annealing to 600640 K was consistent with the diffusion of Ni into the subsurface region of Pt(111); the possibility of the production of the PtNiPt(111) structure, with Ni atoms staying directly underneath the surface Pt, was further suggested from the DFT modeling and experimental measurements of chemical properties. Lattice mismatch results in the contraction or expansion of adlayer metalmetal bond length compared with that of the bulk metal, leading to a modification of the surface electronic properties due to the strain effect [6] ,[10] ,[11] .\"\n          [3] \"In addition, the formation of heterometallic bonds further alters the electronic properties of the surface, which is often referred to as the ligand effect.\"\n          [4] \"One useful parameter to describe the changes in the electronic properties of bimetallic surfaces is the position of the surface d-band center with respect to the Fermi level [12] .\"\n          [5] \"This parameter has been shown to strongly correlate with the ability of bimetallic surfaces to bind with small adsorbates, such as atomic hydrogen and oxygen [13] , alkenes [8] ,[14] , and oxygenates [15] ,[16] .\"\n          [6] \"In addition, activation barriers to such reactions as ethylene and maleic anhydride hydrogenation also have been correlated with the surface d-band center [8] ,[17] .\"\n          [7] \"Thus, its determination may enable first-principles predictions of bimetallic surfaces with desirable catalytic properties for reactions involving these molecules [18] .\"\n          [8] \"In the present work, a combination of density functional theory (DFT) modeling and surface science experiments was used to study the effects of bimetallic formation on the binding of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene, as well as on the low-temperature hydrogenation of cyclohexene.\"\n          [9] \"This was done by modifying Pt(111) with several 3d transition metals, including Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu.\"\n          [10] \"Depositing these metals on a Pt(111) single-crystal surface at room temperature was found to result in the formation of a surface monolayer of the 3d metals; however, when Pt(111) is modified with another metal, the dominant reaction pathways can vary markedly.\"\n          [20] \"For example, modification with Sn can promote reversible adsorption, making molecular desorption the dominant pathway.\"\n          [21] \"Previous studies on 3d-modified Pt(111) have shown that the subsurface Pt-Ni-Pt(111) and Pt-Co-Pt(111) structures exhibit a novel low-temperature hydrogenation pathway [28] ,[31] ,[32] .\"\n          [22] \"Similar results were observed in the current study for the Pt-Fe-Pt(111) surface; the boat and chair configurations were calculated, demonstrating that the boat configuration is the thermodynamically preferred structure for di-σ bonded cyclohexene.\"", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using a combination of density functional theory (DFT) modeling and surface science experiments. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research. The unique properties of bimetallic surfaces often result in activities and selectivities that exceed those of monometallic catalysts. Fundamental experimental and theoretical studies have been conducted to explore the novel properties of well-defined bimetallic surfaces. A monolayer film of one metal can be deposited onto a single-crystal substrate of another metal to study the modification effects on surface chemistry due to bimetallic formation. Lattice mismatch leads to a modification of the surface electronic properties due to the strain effect, and the formation of heterometallic bonds further alters the electronic properties of the surface, known as the ligand effect. The position of the surface d-band center with respect to the Fermi level is a useful parameter to describe the changes in the electronic properties of bimetallic surfaces, which has been shown to correlate with the ability of bimetallic surfaces to bind with small adsorbates and activation barriers to reactions. Determination of the surface d-band center may enable first-principles predictions of bimetallic surfaces with desirable catalytic properties. In the present work, a combination of DFT modeling and surface science experiments was used to study the effects of bimetallic formation on the binding of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene, as well as on the low-temperature hydrogenation of cyclohexene. Pt(111) was modified with several 3d transition metals, including Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu. Depositing these metals on a Pt(111) single-crystal surface at room temperature resulted in the formation of a surface monolayer of the 3d metals, designated as 3d-Pt-Pt(111). At elevated temperatures, the formation of a surface alloy was observed for each Pt-3d pair, enriched in Pt in the first atomic layer due to the enthalpic driving potential created by the lower surface energy of Pt compared with the 3d metals under consideration. Strain may play a part in the interdiffusion of the Pt and 3d metals, and these Pt-enriched bimetallic surfaces are designated Pt-3d-Pt(111) in this study. Kitchin et al. studied Ni modification of Pt(111) and found that surface Ni shifts the surface d-band center closer to the Fermi level in comparison to Ni(111), whereas subsurface Ni in the second atomic layer moves the d-band center away from the Fermi level. The current study extends these findings to Fe-, Co-, and Cu-modified Pt(111) surfaces. Cyclohexene is an ideal probe molecule for comparing the general trends in the chemical properties of the various bimetallic surfaces due to the competitive nature of its reaction pathways. Previous studies have shown that subsurface Pt-Ni-Pt(111) and Pt-Co-Pt(111) structures exhibit a novel low-temperature hydrogenation pathway, and similar results were observed in the current study for the Pt-Fe-Pt(111) surface. However, the Pt-Cu-Pt(111) surface did not exhibit the same hydrogenation pathway. The hydrogenation pathway did not occur on the 3d-Pt-Pt(111) surfaces due to the strong binding of cyclohexene and atomic hydrogen. The combined experimental results and DFT modeling allow for the establishment of a volcano-type relationship between the binding energies and hydrogenation activities among the various 3d/Pt(111) bimetallic surfaces. The study was extended to the growth and thermal behavior of Fe and Cu on the Pt(111) surface. The surfaces were prepared by depositing 1 ML of the 3d metal at 300 K for the surface configuration, and at 600 K for the subsurface bimetallic configuration. DFT was used to calculate the binding energies of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene on the monometallic and bimetallic surfaces. The binding energies of both the boat and chair configurations were calculated for di-σ bonded cyclohexene, demonstrating that the boat configuration is the thermodynamically preferred structure. The study was performed in a two-level stainless steel ultra-high vacuum (UHV) chamber equipped with an Auger electron spectrometer (AES) and a quadrupole mass spectrometer (MS) for temperature-programmed desorption (TPD) experiments and in-situ verification of the purity of the dosed gases. The surfaces were modified by depositing a 3d metal using physical vapor deposition, and the quantity of 3d metal deposited was determined by the 3d (LMM)/Pt (241 eV) AES peak-to-peak ratio. The AES quantification of the physical vapor deposition and thermal behavior of Fe and Cu on Pt(111) was performed. The surfaces were heated at 3 K/s to increasingly high temperatures, and AES scans were performed once the surfaces were cooled to below 500 K, to determine changes in the surface composition. The surfaces used in the current study were pseudomorphic films of Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu, for which approximately five to ten monolayers of the 3d metal were deposited on Pt(111) such that Pt was barely detectable in the AES scan. The thin film surfaces were modeled as the bulk closed packed 3d surface for each respective metal. The theoretical results presented in this paper were calculated using self-consistent periodic slab calculations with the VASP (Vienna ab initio Simulation Package) code. The binding energies of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene were studied using super cells containing four atomic layers, with the top two layers allowed to relax in each case. Calculations for gas-phase hydrogen and cyclohexene were carried out implementing spin-polarization, whereas the adsorbate-metal system calculations were carried out spin-unpolarized, because the relative difference in the adsorption energies with and without spin-polarization was typically found to be <5 kJ/mol for atomic hydrogen and alkenes. For the hydrogen-metal system, hydrogen was adsorbed in the threefold hollow site of the metal surface with a coverage of 1/9 ML. The binding of cyclohexene was studied on hydrogen co-adsorbed surfaces. One cyclohexene molecule was bonded in the di-σ configuration on the monometallic and bimetallic surfaces, with the presence of two co-adsorbed hydrogen atoms in the super cell. The hydrogen atoms were bonded in the two threefold hollow sites nearest to the cyclohexene molecule, to ascertain the effect of repulsion on the binding of cyclohexene.", "Chinese": "Ni/Pt双金属表面的表征，通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层制备，采用密度泛函理论(DFT)建模和表面科学实验的组合进行。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要，这些表面在高级表面科学和催化研究的背景下。双金属表面的独特性质通常导致活性和选择性超过单金属催化剂。已经进行了许多基础实验和理论研究，以探索定义良好的双金属表面的新型性质。为了研究双金属形成对表面化学的修改效应，可以在另一种金属的单晶基底上沉积一层金属薄膜。晶格失配导致由于应变效应，表面电子性质的修改，而异金属键的形成进一步改变了表面的电子性质，这通常被称为配体效应。描述双金属表面电子性质变化的一个有用参数是表面d带中心相对于费米能级的位置。已经表明，双金属表面与小吸附物结合的能力与双金属表面的表面d带中心位置密切相关。此外，乙烯和马来酸酐氢化等反应的活化能垒也与表面d带中心相关。因此，确定表面d带中心可能使我们能够从第一原理预测具有所需催化性质的双金属表面，用于涉及这些分子的反应。在本研究中，结合密度泛函理论(DFT)建模和表面科学实验，研究了双金属形成对原子氢和环己烯结合以及环己烯低温氢化的影响。通过在Pt(111)上修饰几种3d过渡金属，包括Fe、Co、Ni和Cu，来实现这一点。在室温下将这些金属沉积在Pt(111)单晶表面上，发现形成了3d金属的表面单层；这些表面被指定为3d-Pt-Pt(111)。在较高温度下，观察到每个Pt-3d对的表面合金的形成，由于与考虑的3d金属相比，Pt的表面能较低，因此在第一原子层中Pt的含量较高。应变也可能在Pt和3d金属的相互扩散中发挥作用，因为较大的Pt原子在最上层原子层中可以减少弹性应变。这些Pt富集的双金属表面在本研究中被指定为Pt-3d-Pt(111)。Kitchin等人研究了Ni对Pt(111)的改性，发现表面Ni与Ni(111)相比，将表面d带中心移近费米能级，而第二原子层中的子表面Ni将d带中心移离费米能级。本研究将这些发现扩展到Fe、Co和Cu改性的Pt(111)表面。环己烯是一种理想的探针分子，用于比较各种双金属表面化学性质的一般趋势，因为其反应途径的竞争性质。先前的研究表明，次表面Pt-Ni-Pt(111)和Pt-Co-Pt(111)结构表现出一种新的低温氢化途径，而在当前的研究中，对于Pt-Fe-Pt(111)表面观察到了类似的结果。然而，Pt-Cu-Pt(111)表面没有表现出相同的氢化途径。由于环己烯和原子氢的强结合，氢化途径没有发生在3d-Pt-Pt(111)表面上。实验结果和DFT建模的结合使我们能够在各种3d/Pt(111)双金属表面之间建立结合能和氢化活性的火山型关系。研究扩展到了Fe和Cu在Pt(111)表面上的生长和热行为。表面通过在300 K下沉积1 ML的3d金属来制备表面配置，而在600 K下制备了次表面双金属配置。DFT用于计算单金属和双金属表面上原子氢和环己烯的结合能。计算了二-σ键合环己烯的船和椅构型的结合能，证明船构型是热力学上优选的结构。研究在配备有Auger电子能谱仪(AES)和四极质谱仪(MS)的两级不锈钢超高压(UHV)室中进行，用于温度编程脱附(TPD)实验和所加气体纯度的原位验证。表面通过物理气相沉积沉积3d金属进行改性，3d金属沉积量由3d (LMM)/Pt (241 eV) AES峰峰值比确定。Fe和Cu在Pt(111)上的物理气相沉积和热行为的AES量化已经完成。表面以3 K/s的速率加热到越来越高的温度，一旦表面冷却到500 K以下，就进行AES扫描，以确定表面组成的变化。目前研究中使用的表面是Fe、Co、Ni和Cu的伪多形薄膜，其中大约5到10个单层的3d金属沉积在Pt(111)上，使得Pt在AES扫描中几乎检测不到。薄膜表面被建模为每个相应金属的紧密堆积3d表面。本文中提出的理论结果使用VASP(维也纳ab initio模拟包)代码进行自洽周期性板计算。使用包含四层原子的超单元研究了原子氢和环己烯的结合能，其中允许顶层的两层松弛。对于气相氢和环己烯的计算实施了自旋极化，而吸附物-金属系统计算则以自旋非极化进行，因为对于原子氢和烯烃，有和没有自旋极化的吸附能的相对差异通常发现<5 kJ/mol。对于氢-金属系统，氢在金属表面的三重空位位置吸附，覆盖率为1/9 ML。在氢共吸附表面上研究了环己烯的结合。一个环己烯分子以二-σ构型键合在单金属和双金属表面上，超单元中存在两个共吸附的氢原子。氢原子键合在最接近环己烯分子的两个三重空位位置，以确定对环己烯结合的影响。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2008.05.013"},
{"Quotes": "", "English": "The literature does not provide information on the characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research because it allows for the correlation of changes in surface structure and related electronic states with chemical reactivity upon the addition of a second constituent. The characterization involves XPS, LEED, UPS, and TPD techniques to investigate the growth mode, electronic structure, and chemical reactivity of the Pt films.", "Chinese": "文献没有提供在Pt(111)单晶或Pt多晶基底上沉积Ni单层制备Ni/Pt双金属表面的表征信息。但是，它确实讨论了通过将Pt原子沉积到Ni(100)表面上来制备模型双金属表面的过程，这是理解PtNi双金属表面的基本特性和反应性的一种替代方法。这个过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面在高级表面科学和催化研究背景下的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要，因为它允许在添加第二个组分时，将表面结构和相关电子态的变化与化学反应性相关联。表征涉及XPS、LEED、UPS和TPD技术，以研究Pt薄膜的生长模式、电子结构和化学反应性。", "Doi": "10.1016/s0039-6028(00)00978-x"},

{"Quotes": "", "English": "The literature does not provide information on how the characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted. However, it is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research because it allows us to understand the effects of subsurface Ni on the properties of the bimetallic surface. The study of the cyclohexene reaction pathways on Pt/Ni(111) surfaces provides insights into the role of subsurface Ni in inducing low-temperature hydrogenation activity. It also helps to determine the surface structure, electronic properties, and reactivity of the bimetallic surfaces, which is essential for predicting and controlling the catalytic activity and selectivity of these surfaces in various chemical reactions. The combination of experimental data and theoretical calculations enables a comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of the bimetallic surfaces, which is essential for the rational design of advanced catalysts.", "Chinese": "通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层来合成Ni/Pt双金属表面的表征是通过实验技术和理论计算的组合进行的。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们在高级表面科学和催化研究背景下对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要，因为它允许将理论预测与实验数据进行验证。通过比较DFT建模的结果与表面科学实验的结果，研究人员可以深入了解双金属表面的独特化学性质，例如Ni/Pt系统，由于表面Ni和表面Pt原子之间的相互作用，显示出新颖的催化行为。这种相互作用导致表面Pt原子的d带中心的偏移，导致氢和烯烃的吸附能与纯Pt或Ni表面相比降低。DFT和实验技术的结合为合理设计具有改进的活性和选择性的双金属催化剂提供了强大的工具，用于各种化学反应，包括烯烃的低温氢化。在高级表面科学和催化研究的背景下，对通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层制备的Ni/Pt双金属表面进行表征，对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要。这一过程使我们能够确定双金属表面的精确原子结构，这对于准确的DFT计算至关重要。通过Auger电子光谱（AES）、温度程序脱附（TPD）和高分辨率电子能量损失光谱（HREELS）等表征技术获得的结构信息为DFT建模提供了必要的输入。反过来，这种建模帮助我们理解表面的电子性质，如d带中心，这对于预测像氢和乙烯这样的分子的吸附能至关重要。实验表征和理论计算的结合使我们能够更深入地理解双金属表面的催化性质，从而促进具有改进的活性和选择性的催化剂的合理设计。通过一系列先进的表面科学技术和理论计算，对在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层制备的Ni/Pt双金属表面进行表征。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面在高级表面科学和催化研究背景下的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要。从表面科学技术中获得的详细结构信息允许对双金属表面进行准确建模，这对于DFT计算至关重要。这些计算提供了对双金属表面电子结构和键合特性的洞察，这对于理解其催化性质至关重要。实验数据和理论计算的结合使我们能够全面理解双金属表面的电子和化学性质，这对于合理设计高级催化剂至关重要。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.susc.2005.03.046"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"The Ni /Pt(111) bimetallic surfaces have been characterized using a wide range of experimental techniques and DFT modeling [26] . When Ni is deposited with the Pt(111) surface held at 300 K, Ni atoms stay on the topmost layer to produce the NiPt(111) surface MBS structure. If this surface is subsequently heated to 600 K, or if the monolayer deposition occurs with the Pt(111) substrate held at 600 K, most of the Ni atoms diffuse into the subsurface region to produce the PtNiPt(111) subsurface MBS structure.\"\n          [2] \"Below we will use the NiPt(111) and PtNiPt(111) surfaces as model systems to illustrate the information that can be derived from AES, XPS, LEIS and STM characterization.\"\n          [3] \"Fig. 5 shows the LEIS and AES results following the annealing of the 300 K NiPt(111) surface to 900 K.\"\n          [4] \"Fig. 6 shows the normal and grazing emission XPS of the NiPt(111) surface prepared at 300 K and the PtNiPt(111) subsurface structure prepared at 600 K.\"\n          [5] \"Finally, STM was also utilized to further characterize the morphology of the 300 K and 600 K surfaces.\"\n          [6] \"Overall, the AES, LEIS, XPS and STM results confirmed the presence of a surface Ni monolayer on Pt(111) after the deposition of Ni at 300 K.\"\n          [7] \"The characterization following the annealing to 600640 K was consistent with the diffusion of Ni into the subsurface region of Pt(111); the possibility of the production of the PtNiPt(111) structure, with Ni atoms staying directly underneath the surface Pt, was further suggested from the DFT modeling and experimental measurements of chemical properties, as described later.\"", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using a wide range of experimental techniques and DFT modeling. When Ni is deposited with the Pt(111) surface held at 300 K, Ni atoms stay on the topmost layer to produce the NiPt(111) surface MBS structure. If this surface is subsequently heated to 600 K, or if the monolayer deposition occurs with the Pt(111) substrate held at 600 K, most of the Ni atoms diffuse into the subsurface region to produce the PtNiPt(111) subsurface MBS structure. The surfaces are characterized using AES, XPS, LEIS, and STM. The LEIS and AES results following the annealing of the 300 K NiPt(111) surface to 900 K are shown in Fig. 5. The normal and grazing emission XPS of the NiPt(111) surface prepared at 300 K and the PtNiPt(111) subsurface structure prepared at 600 K are shown in Fig. 6. STM was also utilized to further characterize the morphology of the 300 K and 600 K surfaces. The AES, LEIS, XPS, and STM results confirmed the presence of a surface Ni monolayer on Pt(111) after the deposition of Ni at 300 K. The characterization following the annealing to 600640 K was consistent with the diffusion of Ni into the subsurface region of Pt(111); the possibility of the production of the PtNiPt(111) structure, with Ni atoms staying directly underneath the surface Pt, was further suggested from the DFT modeling and experimental measurements of chemical properties. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research.", "Chinese": "通过在300 K下将Ni沉积在Pt(111)表面上，Ni原子停留在最顶层，形成NiPt(111)表面MBS结构。如果随后将该表面加热至600 K，或者在600 K下将Pt(111)基板进行单层沉积，大多数Ni原子会扩散到Pt(111)的次表面区域，形成PtNiPt(111)次表面MBS结构。使用AES、XPS、LEIS和STM对Ni/Pt双金属表面进行表征。图5显示了将300 K NiPt(111)表面加热至900 K后的LEIS和AES结果。图6显示了在300 K下制备的NiPt(111)表面和在600 K下制备的PtNiPt(111)次表面结构的正常和掠射发射XPS。STM也被用来进一步表征300 K和600 K表面的形貌。AES、LEIS、XPS和STM结果证实，在300 K下沉积Ni后，Pt(111)表面存在一层Ni单层。在600640 K下退火后的表征与Ni扩散到Pt(111)的次表面区域一致；从DFT建模和化学性质的实验测量中进一步提出了PtNiPt(111)结构的可能性，其中Ni原子直接位于表面Pt下方。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面在高级表面科学和催化研究背景下的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.surfrep.2008.02.001"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"In many cases, these unique properties result in activities and/or selectivities that exceed those achievable with a monometallic catalyst. For this reason, there have been many fundamental experimental and theoretical studies of the novel properties of well-defined bimetallic surfaces [2] ,[3] ,[4] ,[5] ,[6] ,[7] ,[8] ,[9] .\"\n          [2] \"To study the modification effects on surface chemistry due to bimetallic formation, a monolayer film of one metal can be deposited onto a single-crystal substrate of another metal. characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using a combination of density functional theory (DFT) modeling and surface science experiments. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research. The unique properties of bimetallic surfaces often result in activities and selectivities that exceed those of monometallic catalysts. Fundamental experimental and theoretical studies have been conducted to explore the novel properties of well-defined bimetallic surfaces. A monolayer film of one metal can be deposited onto a single-crystal substrate of another metal to study the modification effects on surface chemistry due to bimetallic formation. Lattice mismatch leads to a modification of the surface electronic properties due to the strain effect, and the formation of heterometallic bonds further alters the electronic properties of the surface, known as the ligand effect. The position of the surface d-band center with respect to the Fermi level is a useful parameter to describe the changes in the electronic properties of bimetallic surfaces, which has been shown to correlate with the ability of bimetallic surfaces to bind with small adsorbates and activation barriers to reactions. Determination of the surface d-band center may enable first-principles predictions of bimetallic surfaces with desirable catalytic properties. In the present work, a combination of DFT modeling and surface science experiments was used to study the effects of bimetallic formation on the binding of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene, as well as on the low-temperature hydrogenation of cyclohexene. Pt(111) was modified with several 3d transition metals, including Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu. Depositing these metals on a Pt(111) single-crystal surface at room temperature resulted in the formation of a surface monolayer of the 3d metals, designated as 3d-Pt-Pt(111). At elevated temperatures, the formation of a surface alloy was observed for each Pt-3d pair, enriched in Pt in the first atomic layer due to the enthalpic driving potential created by the lower surface energy of Pt compared with the 3d metals under consideration. Strain may play a part in the interdiffusion of the Pt and 3d metals, and these Pt-enriched bimetallic surfaces are designated Pt-3d-Pt(111) in this study. Kitchin et al. studied Ni modification of Pt(111) and found that surface Ni shifts the surface d-band center closer to the Fermi level in comparison to Ni(111), whereas subsurface Ni in the second atomic layer moves the d-band center away from the Fermi level. The current study extends these findings to Fe-, Co-, and Cu-modified Pt(111) surfaces. Cyclohexene is an ideal probe molecule for comparing the general trends in the chemical properties of the various bimetallic surfaces due to the competitive nature of its reaction pathways. Previous studies have shown that subsurface Pt-Ni-Pt(111) and Pt-Co-Pt(111) structures exhibit a novel low-temperature hydrogenation pathway, and similar results were observed in the current study for the Pt-Fe-Pt(111) surface. However, the Pt-Cu-Pt(111) surface did not exhibit the same hydrogenation pathway. The hydrogenation pathway did not occur on the 3d-Pt-Pt(111) surfaces due to the strong binding of cyclohexene and atomic hydrogen. The combined experimental results and DFT modeling allow for the establishment of a volcano-type relationship between the binding energies and hydrogenation activities among the various 3d/Pt(111) bimetallic surfaces. The study was extended to the growth and thermal behavior of Fe and Cu on the Pt(111) surface. The surfaces were prepared by depositing 1 ML of the 3d metal at 300 K for the surface configuration, and at 600 K for the subsurface bimetallic configuration. DFT was used to calculate the binding energies of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene on the monometallic and bimetallic surfaces. The binding energies of both the boat and chair configurations were calculated for di-σ bonded cyclohexene, demonstrating that the boat configuration is the thermodynamically preferred structure. The study was performed in a two-level stainless steel ultra-high vacuum (UHV) chamber equipped with an Auger electron spectrometer (AES) and a quadrupole mass spectrometer (MS) for temperature-programmed desorption (TPD) experiments and in-situ verification of the purity of the dosed gases. The surfaces were modified by depositing a 3d metal using physical vapor deposition, and the quantity of 3d metal deposited was determined by the 3d (LMM)/Pt (241 eV) AES peak-to-peak ratio. The AES quantification of the physical vapor deposition and thermal behavior of Fe and Cu on Pt(111) was performed. The surfaces were heated at 3 K/s to increasingly high temperatures, and AES scans were performed once the surfaces were cooled to below 500 K, to determine changes in the surface composition. The surfaces used in the current study were pseudomorphic films of Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu, for which approximately five to ten monolayers of the 3d metal were deposited on Pt(111) such that Pt was barely detectable in the AES scan. The thin film surfaces were modeled as the bulk closed packed 3d surface for each respective metal. The theoretical results presented in this paper were calculated using self-consistent periodic slab calculations with the VASP (Vienna ab initio Simulation Package) code. The binding energies of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene were studied using super cells containing four atomic layers, with the top two layers allowed to relax in each case. Calculations for gas-phase hydrogen and cyclohexene were carried out implementing spin-polarization, whereas the adsorbate-metal system calculations were carried out spin-unpolarized, because the relative difference in the adsorption energies with and without spin-polarization was typically found to be <5 kJ/mol for atomic hydrogen and alkenes. For the hydrogen-metal system, hydrogen was adsorbed in the threefold hollow site of the metal surface with a coverage of 1/9 ML. The binding of cyclohexene was studied on hydrogen co-adsorbed surfaces. One cyclohexene molecule was bonded in the di-σ configuration on the monometallic and bimetallic surfaces, with the presence of two co-adsorbed hydrogen atoms in the super cell. The hydrogen atoms were bonded in the two threefold hollow sites nearest to the cyclohexene molecule, to ascertain the effect of repulsion on the binding of cyclohexene.", "Chinese": "Ni/Pt双金属表面的表征，通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层制备，采用密度泛函理论(DFT)建模和表面科学实验的组合进行。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要，这些表面在高级表面科学和催化研究的背景下。双金属表面的独特性质通常导致活性和选择性超过单金属催化剂。已经进行了许多基础实验和理论研究，以探索定义良好的双金属表面的新型性质。为了研究双金属形成对表面化学的修改效应，可以在另一种金属的单晶基底上沉积一层金属薄膜。晶格失配导致由于应变效应，表面电子性质的修改，而异金属键的形成进一步改变了表面的电子性质，这通常被称为配体效应。描述双金属表面电子性质变化的一个有用参数是表面d带中心相对于费米能级的位置。已经表明，双金属表面与小吸附物结合的能力与双金属表面的表面d带中心位置密切相关。此外，乙烯和马来酸酐氢化等反应的活化能垒也与表面d带中心相关。因此，确定表面d带中心可能使我们能够从第一原理预测具有所需催化性质的双金属表面，用于涉及这些分子的反应。在本研究中，结合密度泛函理论(DFT)建模和表面科学实验，研究了双金属形成对原子氢和环己烯结合以及环己烯低温氢化的影响。通过在Pt(111)上修饰几种3d过渡金属，包括Fe、Co、Ni和Cu，来实现这一点。在室温下将这些金属沉积在Pt(111)单晶表面上，发现形成了3d金属的表面单层；这些表面被指定为3d-Pt-Pt(111)。在较高温度下，观察到每个Pt-3d对的表面合金的形成，由于与考虑的3d金属相比，Pt的表面能较低，因此在第一原子层中Pt的含量较高。应变也可能在Pt和3d金属的相互扩散中发挥作用，因为较大的Pt原子在最上层原子层中可以减少弹性应变。这些Pt富集的双金属表面在本研究中被指定为Pt-3d-Pt(111)。Kitchin等人研究了Ni对Pt(111)的改性，发现表面Ni与Ni(111)相比，将表面d带中心移近费米能级，而第二原子层中的子表面Ni将d带中心移离费米能级。本研究将这些发现扩展到Fe、Co和Cu改性的Pt(111)表面。环己烯是一种理想的探针分子，用于比较各种双金属表面化学性质的一般趋势，因为其反应途径的竞争性质。先前的研究表明，次表面Pt-Ni-Pt(111)和Pt-Co-Pt(111)结构表现出一种新的低温氢化途径，而在当前的研究中，对于Pt-Fe-Pt(111)表面观察到了类似的结果。然而，Pt-Cu-Pt(111)表面没有表现出相同的氢化途径。由于环己烯和原子氢的强结合，氢化途径没有发生在3d-Pt-Pt(111)表面上。实验结果和DFT建模的结合使我们能够在各种3d/Pt(111)双金属表面之间建立结合能和氢化活性的火山型关系。研究扩展到了Fe和Cu在Pt(111)表面上的生长和热行为。表面通过在300 K下沉积1 ML的3d金属来制备表面配置，而在600 K下制备了次表面双金属配置。DFT用于计算单金属和双金属表面上原子氢和环己烯的结合能。计算了二-σ键合环己烯的船和椅构型的结合能，证明船构型是热力学上优选的结构。研究在配备有Auger电子能谱仪(AES)和四极质谱仪(MS)的两级不锈钢超高压(UHV)室中进行，用于温度编程脱附(TPD)实验和所加气体纯度的原位验证。表面通过物理气相沉积沉积3d金属进行改性，3d金属沉积量由3d (LMM)/Pt (241 eV) AES峰峰值比确定。Fe和Cu在Pt(111)上的物理气相沉积和热行为的AES量化已经完成。表面以3 K/s的速率加热到越来越高的温度，一旦表面冷却到500 K以下，就进行AES扫描，以确定表面组成的变化。目前研究中使用的表面是Fe、Co、Ni和Cu的伪多形薄膜，其中大约5到10个单层的3d金属沉积在Pt(111)上，使得Pt在AES扫描中几乎检测不到。薄膜表面被建模为每个相应金属的紧密堆积3d表面。本文中提出的理论结果使用VASP(维也纳ab ML。在氢共吸附表面上研究了环己烯的结合。一个环己烯分子以二-σ构型键合在单金属和双金属表面上，超单元中存在两个共吸附的氢原子。氢原子键合在最接近环己烯分子的两个三重空位位置，以确定对环己烯结合的影响。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2008.05.013"},

{"Quotes": "", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using low-energy electron diffraction (LEED) and Auger electron spectroscopy (AES). This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research because it allows us to observe the initial growth and the alloy formation of Ni ultrathin films on Pt(111) surface. Several interesting structural phases were observed in this system: pseudo-(1×1), coherent epitaxy, incoherent epitaxy, and (2×2). The phase diagram was determined by LEED. In addition, the formation of NiPt alloy was investigated at various Ni coverages. {"Quotes": "[1] \"In many cases, these unique properties result in activities and/or selectivities that exceed those achievable with a monometallic catalyst. the boat and chair configurations were calculated, demonstrating that the boat configuration is the thermodynamically preferred structure for di-σ bonded cyclohexene.\"", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using a combination of density functional theory (DFT) modeling and surface science experiments. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research. The unique properties of bimetallic surfaces often result in activities and selectivities that exceed those of monometallic catalysts. Fundamental experimental and theoretical studies have been conducted to explore the novel properties of well-defined bimetallic surfaces. A monolayer film of one metal can be deposited onto a single-crystal substrate of another metal to study the modification effects on surface chemistry due to bimetallic formation. Lattice mismatch leads to a modification of the surface electronic properties due to the strain effect, and the formation of heterometallic bonds further alters the electronic properties of the surface, known as the ligand effect. The position of the surface d-band center with respect to the Fermi level is a useful parameter to describe the changes in the electronic properties of bimetallic surfaces, which has been shown to correlate with the ability of bimetallic surfaces to bind with small adsorbates and activation barriers to reactions. Determination of the surface d-band center may enable first-principles predictions of bimetallic surfaces with desirable catalytic properties. In the present work, a combination of DFT modeling and surface science experiments was used to study the effects of bimetallic formation on the binding of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene, as well as on the low-temperature hydrogenation of cyclohexene. Pt(111) was modified with several 3d transition metals, including Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu. Depositing these metals on a Pt(111) single-crystal surface at room temperature resulted in the formation of a surface monolayer of the 3d metals, designated as 3d-Pt-Pt(111). At elevated temperatures, the formation of a surface alloy was observed for each Pt-3d pair, enriched in Pt in the first atomic layer due to the enthalpic driving potential created by the lower surface energy of Pt compared with the 3d metals under consideration. Strain may play a part in the interdiffusion of the Pt and 3d metals, and these Pt-enriched bimetallic surfaces are designated Pt-3d-Pt(111) in this study. Kitchin et al. studied Ni modification of Pt(111) and found that surface Ni shifts the surface d-band center closer to the Fermi level in comparison to Ni(111), whereas subsurface Ni in the second atomic layer moves the d-band center away from the Fermi level. The current study extends these findings to Fe-, Co-, and Cu-modified Pt(111) surfaces. Cyclohexene is an ideal probe molecule for comparing the general trends in the chemical properties of the various bimetallic surfaces due to the competitive nature of its reaction pathways. Previous studies have shown that subsurface Pt-Ni-Pt(111) and Pt-Co-Pt(111) structures exhibit a novel low-temperature hydrogenation pathway, and similar results were observed in the current study for the Pt-Fe-Pt(111) surface. However, the Pt-Cu-Pt(111) surface did not exhibit the same hydrogenation pathway. The hydrogenation pathway did not occur on the 3d-Pt-Pt(111) surfaces due to the strong binding of cyclohexene and atomic hydrogen. The combined experimental results and DFT modeling allow for the establishment of a volcano-type relationship between the binding energies and hydrogenation activities among the various 3d/Pt(111) bimetallic surfaces. The study was extended to the growth and thermal behavior of Fe and Cu on the Pt(111) surface. The surfaces were prepared by depositing 1 ML of the 3d metal at 300 K for the surface configuration, and at 600 K for the subsurface bimetallic configuration. DFT was used to calculate the binding energies of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene on the monometallic and bimetallic surfaces. The binding energies of both the boat and chair configurations were calculated for di-σ bonded cyclohexene, demonstrating that the boat configuration is the thermodynamically preferred structure. The study was performed in a two-level stainless steel ultra-high vacuum (UHV) chamber equipped with an Auger electron spectrometer (AES) and a quadrupole mass spectrometer (MS) for temperature-programmed desorption (TPD) experiments and in-situ verification of the purity of the dosed gases. The surfaces were modified by depositing a 3d metal using physical vapor deposition, and the quantity of 3d metal deposited was determined by the 3d (LMM)/Pt (241 eV) AES peak-to-peak ratio. The AES quantification of the physical vapor deposition and thermal behavior of Fe and Cu on Pt(111) was performed. The surfaces were heated at 3 K/s to increasingly high temperatures, and AES scans were performed once the surfaces were cooled to below 500 K, to determine changes in the surface composition. The surfaces used in the current study were pseudomorphic films of Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu, for which approximately five to ten monolayers of the 3d metal were deposited on Pt(111) such that Pt was barely detectable in the AES scan. The thin film surfaces were modeled as the bulk closed packed 3d surface for each respective metal. The theoretical results presented in this paper were calculated using self-consistent periodic slab calculations with the VASP (Vienna ab initio Simulation Package) code. The binding energies of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene were studied using super cells containing four atomic layers, with the top two layers allowed to relax in each case. Calculations for gas-phase hydrogen and cyclohexene were carried out implementing spin-polarization, whereas the adsorbate-metal system calculations were carried out spin-unpolarized, because the relative difference in the adsorption energies with and without spin-polarization was typically found to be <5 kJ/mol for atomic hydrogen and alkenes. For the hydrogen-metal system, hydrogen was adsorbed in the threefold hollow site of the metal surface with a coverage of 1/9 ML. The binding of cyclohexene was studied on hydrogen co-adsorbed surfaces. One cyclohexene molecule was bonded in the di-σ configuration on the monometallic and bimetallic surfaces, with the presence of two co-adsorbed hydrogen atoms in the super cell. The hydrogen atoms were bonded in the two threefold hollow sites nearest to the cyclohexene molecule, to ascertain the effect of repulsion on the binding of cyclohexene.", "Chinese": "Ni/Pt双金属表面的表征，通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层制备，采用密度泛函理论(DFT)建模和表面科学实验的组合进行。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要，这些表面在高级表面科学和催化研究的背景下。双金属表面的独特性质通常导致活性和选择性超过单金属催化剂。已经进行了许多基础实验和理论研究，以探索定义良好的双金属表面的新型性质。为了研究双金属形成对表面化学的修改效应，可以在另一种金属的单晶基底上沉积一层金属薄膜。晶格失配导致由于应变效应，表面电子性质的修改，而异金属键的形成进一步改变了表面的电子性质，这通常被称为配体效应。描述双金属表面电子性质变化的一个有用参数是表面d带中心相对于费米能级的位置。已经表明，双金属表面与小吸附物结合的能力与双金属表面的表面d带中心位置密切相关。此外，乙烯和马来酸酐氢化等反应的活化能垒也与表面d带中心相关。因此，确定表面d带中心可能使我们能够从第一原理预测具有所需催化性质的双金属表面，用于涉及这些分子的反应。在本研究中，结合密度泛函理论(DFT)建模和表面科学实验，研究了双金属形成对原子氢和环己烯结合以及环己烯低温氢化的影响。通过在Pt(111)上修饰几种3d过渡金属，包括Fe、Co、Ni和Cu，来实现这一点。在室温下将这些金属沉积在Pt(111)单晶表面上，发现形成了3d金属的表面单层；这些表面被指定为3d-Pt-Pt(111)。在较高温度下，观察到每个Pt-3d对的表面合金的形成，由于与考虑的3d金属相比，Pt的表面能较低，因此在第一原子层中Pt的含量较高。应变也可能在Pt和3d金属的相互扩散中发挥作用，因为较大的Pt原子在最上层原子层中可以减少弹性应变。这些Pt富集的双金属表面在本研究中被指定为Pt-3d-Pt(111)。Kitchin等人研究了Ni对Pt(111)的改性，发现表面Ni与Ni(111)相比，将表面d带中心移近费米能级，而第二原子层中的子表面Ni将d带中心移离费米能级。本研究将这些发现扩展到Fe、Co和Cu改性的Pt(111)表面。环己烯是一种理想的探针分子，用于比较各种双金属表面化学性质的一般趋势，因为其反应途径的竞争性质。先前的研究表明，次表面Pt-Ni-Pt(111)和Pt-Co-Pt(111)结构表现出一种新的低温氢化途径，而在当前的研究中，对于Pt-Fe-Pt(111)表面观察到了类似的结果。然而，Pt-Cu-Pt(111)表面没有表现出相同的氢化途径。由于环己烯和原子氢的强结合，氢化途径没有发生在3d-Pt-Pt(111)表面上。实验结果和DFT建模的结合使我们能够在各种3d/Pt(111)双金属表面之间建立结合能和氢化活性的火山型关系。研究扩展到了Fe和Cu在Pt(111)表面上的生长和热行为。表面通过在300 K下沉积1 ML的3d金属来制备表面配置，而在600 K下制备了次表面双金属配置。DFT用于计算单金属和双金属表面上原子氢和环己烯的结合能。计算了二-σ键合环己烯的船和椅构型的结合能，证明船构型是热力学上优选的结构。研究在配备有Auger电子能谱仪(AES)和四极质谱仪(MS)的两级不锈钢超高压(UHV)室中进行，用于温度编程脱附(TPD)实验和所加气体纯度的原位验证。表面通过物理气相沉积沉积3d金属进行改性，3d金属沉积量由3d (LMM)/Pt (241 eV) AES峰峰值比确定。Fe和Cu在Pt(111)上的物理气相沉积和热行为的AES量化已经完成。表面以3 K/s的速率加热到越来越高的温度，一旦表面冷却到500 K以下，就进行AES扫描，以确定表面组成的变化。目前研究中使用的表面是Fe、Co、Ni和Cu的伪多形薄膜，其中大约5到10个单层的3d金属沉积在Pt(111)上，使得Pt在AES扫描中几乎检测不到。薄膜表面被建模为每个相应金属的紧密堆积3d表面。本文中提出的理论结果使用VASP(维也纳ab initio模拟包)代码进行自洽周期性板计算。使用包含四层原子的超单元研究了原子氢和环己烯的结合能，其中允许顶层的两层松弛。对于气相氢和环己烯的计算实施了自旋极化，而吸附物-金属系统计算则以自旋非极化进行，因为对于原子氢和烯烃，有和没有自旋极化的吸附能的相对差异通常发现<5 kJ/mol。对于氢-金属系统，氢在金属表面的三重空位位置吸附，覆盖率为1/9 ML。在氢共吸附表面上研究了环己烯的结合。一个环己烯分子以二-σ构型键合在单金属和双金属表面上，超单元中存在两个共吸附的氢原子。氢原子键合在最接近环己烯分子的两个三重空位位置，以确定对环己烯结合的影响。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2008.05.013"},

{"Quotes": "", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is not explicitly described in the literature. However, the process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research because it allows for the investigation of the influence of structural parameters on catalytic activity and magnetism of an alloy. The NiPt system is an interesting candidate for investigations due to its high catalytic selectivity for certain reactions and the strong interplay between magnetic and spatial order. It also allows for the investigation of atomic scale interactions and the formation of metastable alloy phases. The study shows that Ni atoms exchange with Pt at both terrace and step sites, forming a one-dimensional ordered alloy at the step edges and randomly embedding in Pt on the terraces. At higher temperatures, a 2x2 substitutional alloy is formed, corresponding to a Ni20Pt80 composition of the surface topmost layer. {"Quotes": "", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using low-energy electron diffraction (LEED) and Auger electron spectroscopy (AES). {"Quotes": "[1] \"In many cases, these unique properties result in activities and/or selectivities that exceed those achievable with a monometallic catalyst. For this reason, there have been many fundamental experimental and theoretical studies of the novel properties of well-defined bimetallic surfaces [2] ,[3] ,[4] ,[5] ,[6] ,[7] ,[8] ,[9] .\"\n          [2] \"To study the modification effects on surface chemistry due to bimetallic formation, a monolayer film of one metal can be deposited onto a single-crystal substrate of another metal. Lattice mismatch results in the contraction or expansion of adlayer metalmetal bond length compared with that of the bulk metal, leading to a modification of the surface electronic properties due to the strain effect [6] ,[10] ,[11] .\"\n          [3] \"In addition, the formation of heterometallic bonds further alters the electronic properties of the surface, which is often referred to as the ligand effect.\"\n          [4] \"One useful parameter to describe the changes in the electronic properties of bimetallic surfaces is the position of the surface d-band center with respect to the Fermi level [12] .\"\n          [5] \"This parameter has been shown to strongly correlate with the ability of bimetallic surfaces to bind with small adsorbates, such as atomic hydrogen and oxygen [13] , alkenes [8] ,[14] , and oxygenates [15] ,[16] .\"\n          [6] \"In addition, activation barriers to such reactions as ethylene and maleic anhydride hydrogenation also have been correlated with the surface d-band center [8] ,[17] .\"\n          [7] \"Thus, its determination may enable first-principles predictions of bimetallic surfaces with desirable catalytic properties for reactions involving these molecules [18] .\"\n          [8] \"In the present work, a combination of density functional theory (DFT) modeling and surface science experiments was used to study the effects of bimetallic formation on the binding of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene, as well as on the low-temperature hydrogenation of cyclohexene.\"\n          [9] \"This was done by modifying Pt(111) with several 3d transition metals, including Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu.\"\n          [10] \"Depositing these metals on a Pt(111) single-crystal surface at room temperature was found to result in the formation of a surface monolayer of the 3d metals; these surfaces are designated as 3d-Pt-Pt(111).\"\n          [11] \"At elevated temperatures, the formation of a surface alloy is observed for each Pt-3d pair [9] ,[19] ,[20] ,[21] ,[22] ,[23] ,[24] ,[25] ,[26] ,[27] .\"\n          [12] \"These surface alloys have been shown to be enriched in Pt in the first atomic layer due to the enthalpic driving potential created by the lower surface energy of Pt compared with the 3d metals under consideration [28] ,[29] .\"\n          [13] \"Strain also may play a part in the interdiffusion of the Pt and 3d metals, because elastic strain is reduced by having the larger Pt atoms in the topmost atomic layer [23] .\"\n          [14] \"These Pt-enriched bimetallic surfaces are designated Pt-3d-Pt(111) in this study.\"\n          [15] \"Kitchin et al. [28] studied Ni modification of Pt(111) and found that surface Ni shifts the surface d-band center closer to the Fermi level in comparison to Ni(111), whereas subsurface Ni in the second atomic layer moves the d-band center away from the Fermi level.\"\n          [16] \"The current study extends these findings to Fe-, Co-, and Cu-modified Pt(111) surfaces.\"\n          [17] \"Cyclohexene can undergo decomposition, dehydrogenation, and self-hydrogenation (disproportionation) reactions, as well as hydrogenation in the presence of co-adsorbed atomic hydrogen.\"\n          [18] \"Due to the competitive nature of these reaction pathways, it is an ideal probe molecule for comparing the general trends in the chemical properties of the various bimetallic surfaces.\"\n          [19] \"On Pt(111), cyclohexene undergoes dehydrogenation and decomposition [7] ,[30] ; however, when Pt(111) is modified with another metal, the dominant reaction pathways can vary markedly.\"\n          [20] \"For example, modification with Sn can promote reversible adsorption, making molecular desorption the dominant pathway.\"\n          [21] \"Previous studies on 3d-modified Pt(111) have shown that the subsurface Pt-Ni-Pt(111) and Pt-Co-Pt(111) structures exhibit a novel low-temperature hydrogenation pathway [28] ,[31] ,[32] .\"\n          [22] \"Similar results were observed in the current study for the Pt-Fe-Pt(111) surface; the boat and chair configurations were calculated, demonstrating that the boat configuration is the thermodynamically preferred structure for di-σ bonded cyclohexene.\"", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using a combination of density functional theory (DFT) modeling and surface science experiments. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research. The unique properties of bimetallic surfaces often result in activities and selectivities that exceed those of monometallic catalysts. Fundamental experimental and theoretical studies have been conducted to explore the novel properties of well-defined bimetallic surfaces. A monolayer film of one metal can be deposited onto a single-crystal substrate of another metal to study the modification effects on surface chemistry due to bimetallic formation. Lattice mismatch leads to a modification of the surface electronic properties due to the strain effect, and the formation of heterometallic bonds further alters the electronic properties of the surface, known as the ligand effect. The position of the surface d-band center with respect to the Fermi level is a useful parameter to describe the changes in the electronic properties of bimetallic surfaces, which has been shown to correlate with the ability of bimetallic surfaces to bind with small adsorbates and activation barriers to reactions. Determination of the surface d-band center may enable first-principles predictions of bimetallic surfaces with desirable catalytic properties. In the present work, a combination of DFT modeling and surface science experiments was used to study the effects of bimetallic formation on the binding of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene, as well as on the low-temperature hydrogenation of cyclohexene. Pt(111) was modified with several 3d transition metals, including Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu. Depositing these metals on a Pt(111) single-crystal surface at room temperature resulted in the formation of a surface monolayer of the 3d metals, designated as 3d-Pt-Pt(111). At elevated temperatures, the formation of a surface alloy was observed for each Pt-3d pair, enriched in Pt in the first atomic layer due to the enthalpic driving potential created by the lower surface energy of Pt compared with the 3d metals under consideration. Strain may play a part in the interdiffusion of the Pt and 3d metals, and these Pt-enriched bimetallic surfaces are designated Pt-3d-Pt(111) in this study. Kitchin et al. studied Ni modification of Pt(111) and found that surface Ni shifts the surface d-band center closer to the Fermi level in comparison to Ni(111), whereas subsurface Ni in the second atomic layer moves the d-band center away from the Fermi level. The current study extends these findings to Fe-, Co-, and Cu-modified Pt(111) surfaces. Cyclohexene is an ideal probe molecule for comparing the general trends in the chemical properties of the various bimetallic surfaces due to the competitive nature of its reaction pathways. Previous studies have shown that subsurface Pt-Ni-Pt(111) and Pt-Co-Pt(111) structures exhibit a novel low-temperature hydrogenation pathway, and similar results were observed in the current study for the Pt-Fe-Pt(111) surface. However, the Pt-Cu-Pt(111) surface did not exhibit the same hydrogenation pathway. The hydrogenation pathway did not occur on the 3d-Pt-Pt(111) surfaces due to the strong binding of cyclohexene and atomic hydrogen. The combined experimental results and DFT modeling allow for the establishment of a volcano-type relationship between the binding energies and hydrogenation activities among the various 3d/Pt(111) bimetallic surfaces. The study was extended to the growth and thermal behavior of Fe and Cu on the Pt(111) surface. The surfaces were prepared by depositing 1 ML of the 3d metal at 300 K for the surface configuration, and at 600 K for the subsurface bimetallic configuration. DFT was used to calculate the binding energies of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene on the monometallic and bimetallic surfaces. The binding energies of both the boat and chair configurations were calculated for di-σ bonded cyclohexene, demonstrating that the boat configuration is the thermodynamically preferred structure. The study was performed in a two-level stainless steel ultra-high vacuum (UHV) chamber equipped with an Auger electron spectrometer (AES) and a quadrupole mass spectrometer (MS) for temperature-programmed desorption (TPD) experiments and in-situ verification of the purity of the dosed gases. The surfaces were modified by depositing a 3d metal using physical vapor deposition, and the quantity of 3d metal deposited was determined by the 3d (LMM)/Pt (241 eV) AES peak-to-peak ratio. The AES quantification of the physical vapor deposition and thermal behavior of Fe and Cu on Pt(111) was performed. The surfaces were heated at 3 K/s to increasingly high temperatures, and AES scans were performed once the surfaces were cooled to below 500 K, to determine changes in the surface composition. The surfaces used in the current study were pseudomorphic films of Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu, for which approximately five to ten monolayers of the 3d metal were deposited on Pt(111) such that Pt was barely detectable in the AES scan. The thin film surfaces were modeled as the bulk closed packed 3d surface for each respective metal. The theoretical results presented in this paper were calculated using self-consistent periodic slab calculations with the VASP (Vienna ab initio Simulation Package) code. The binding energies of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene were studied using super cells containing four atomic layers, with the top two layers allowed to relax in each case. Calculations for gas-phase hydrogen and cyclohexene were carried out implementing spin-polarization, whereas the adsorbate-metal system calculations were carried out spin-unpolarized, because the relative difference in the adsorption energies with and without spin-polarization was typically found to be <5 kJ/mol for atomic hydrogen and alkenes. For the hydrogen-metal system, hydrogen was adsorbed in the threefold hollow site of the metal surface with a coverage of 1/9 ML. The binding of cyclohexene was studied on hydrogen co-adsorbed surfaces. One cyclohexene molecule was bonded in the di-σ configuration on the monometallic and bimetallic surfaces, with the presence of two co-adsorbed hydrogen atoms in the super cell. The hydrogen atoms were bonded in the two threefold hollow sites nearest to the cyclohexene molecule, to ascertain the effect of repulsion on the binding of cyclohexene.", "Chinese": "Ni/Pt双金属表面的表征，通过在Pt(111)单晶或多晶Pt基底上沉积Ni单层制备，采用密度泛函理论(DFT)建模和表面科学实验的组合进行。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要，这些表面在高级表面科学和催化研究的背景下。双金属表面的独特性质通常导致活性和选择性超过单金属催化剂。已经进行了许多基础实验和理论研究，以探索定义良好的双金属表面的新型性质。为了研究双金属形成对表面化学的修改效应，可以在另一种金属的单晶基底上沉积一层金属薄膜。晶格失配导致由于应变效应，表面电子性质的修改，而异金属键的形成进一步改变了表面的电子性质，这通常被称为配体效应。描述双金属表面电子性质变化的一个有用参数是表面d带中心相对于费米能级的位置。已经表明，双金属表面与小吸附物结合的能力与双金属表面的表面d带中心位置密切相关。此外，乙烯和马来酸酐氢化等反应的活化能垒也与表面d带中心相关。因此，确定表面d带中心可能使我们能够从第一原理预测具有所需催化性质的双金属表面，用于涉及这些分子的反应。在本研究中，结合密度泛函理论(DFT)建模和表面科学实验，研究了双金属形成对原子氢和环己烯结合以及环己烯低温氢化的影响。通过在Pt(111)上修饰几种3d过渡金属，包括Fe、Co、Ni和Cu，来实现这一点。在室温下将这些金属沉积在Pt(111)单晶表面上，发现形成了3d金属的表面单层；这些表面被指定为3d-Pt-Pt(111)。在较高温度下，观察到每个Pt-3d对的表面合金的形成，由于与考虑的3d金属相比，Pt的表面能较低，因此在第一原子层中Pt的含量较高。应变也可能在Pt和3d金属的相互扩散中发挥作用，因为较大的Pt原子在最上层原子层中可以减少弹性应变。这些Pt富集的双金属表面在本研究中被指定为Pt-3d-Pt(111)。Kitchin等人研究了Ni对Pt(111)的改性，发现表面Ni与Ni(111)相比，将表面d带中心移近费米能级，而第二原子层中的子表面Ni将d带中心移离费米能级。本研究将这些发现扩展到Fe、Co和Cu改性的Pt(111)表面。环己烯是一种理想的探针分子，用于比较各种双金属表面化学性质的一般趋势，因为其反应途径的竞争性质。先前的研究表明，次表面Pt-Ni-Pt(111)和Pt-Co-Pt(111)结构表现出一种新的低温氢化途径，而在当前的研究中，对于Pt-Fe-Pt(111)表面观察到了类似的结果。然而，Pt-Cu-Pt(111)表面没有表现出相同的氢化途径。由于环己烯和原子氢的强结合，氢化途径没有发生在3d-Pt-Pt(111)表面上。实验结果和DFT建模的结合使我们能够在各种3d/Pt(111)双金属表面之间建立结合能和氢化活性的火山型关系。研究扩展到了Fe和Cu在Pt(111)表面上的生长和热行为。表面通过在300 K下沉积1 ML的3d金属来制备表面配置，而在600 K下制备了次表面双金属配置。DFT用于计算单金属和双金属表面上原子氢和环己烯的结合能。计算了二-σ键合环己烯的船和椅构型的结合能，证明船构型是热力学上优选的结构。研究在配备有Auger电子能谱仪(AES)和四极质谱仪(MS)的两级不锈钢超高压(UHV)室中进行，用于温度编程脱附(TPD)实验和所加气体纯度的原位验证。表面通过物理气相沉积沉积3d金属进行改性，3d金属沉积量由3d (LMM)/Pt (241 eV) AES峰峰值比确定。Fe和Cu在Pt(111)上的物理气相沉积和热行为的AES量化已经完成。表面以3 K/s的速率加热到越来越高的温度，一旦表面冷却到500 K以下，就进行AES扫描，以确定表面组成的变化。目前研究中使用的表面是Fe、Co、Ni和Cu的伪多形薄膜，其中大约5到10个单层的3d金属沉积在Pt(111)上，使得Pt在AES扫描中几乎检测不到。薄膜表面被建模为每个相应金属的紧密堆积3d表面。本文中提出的理论结果使用VASP(维也纳ab initio模拟包)代码进行自洽周期性板计算。使用包含四层原子的超单元研究了原子氢和环己烯的结合能，其中允许顶层的两层松弛。对于气相氢和环己烯的计算实施了自旋极化，而吸附物-金属系统计算则以自旋非极化进行，因为对于原子氢和烯烃，有和没有自旋极化的吸附能的相对差异通常发现<5 kJ/mol。对于氢-金属系统，氢在金属表面的三重空位位置吸附，覆盖率为1/9 ML。在氢共吸附表面上研究了环己烯的结合。一个环己烯分子以二-σ构型键合在单金属和双金属表面上，超单元中存在两个共吸附的氢原子。氢原子键合在最接近环己烯分子的两个三重空位位置，以确定对环己烯结合的影响。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.jcat.2008.05.013"},

{"Quotes": "", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research. If this surface is subsequently heated to 600 K, or if the monolayer deposition occurs with the Pt(111) substrate held at 600 K, most of the Ni atoms diffuse into the subsurface region to produce the PtNiPt(111) subsurface MBS structure.\"\n          [2] \"Below we will use the NiPt(111) and PtNiPt(111) surfaces as model systems to illustrate the information that can be derived from AES, XPS, LEIS and STM characterization.\"\n          [3] \"Fig. 5 shows the LEIS and AES results following the annealing of the 300 K NiPt(111) surface to 900 K.\"\n          [4] \"Fig. 6 shows the normal and grazing emission XPS of the NiPt(111) surface prepared at 300 K and the PtNiPt(111) subsurface structure prepared at 600 K.\"\n          [5] \"Finally, STM was also utilized to further characterize the morphology of the 300 K and 600 K surfaces.\"\n          [6] \"Overall, the AES, LEIS, XPS and STM results confirmed the presence of a surface Ni monolayer on Pt(111) after the deposition of Ni at 300 K.\"\n          [7] \"The characterization following the annealing to 600640 K was consistent with the diffusion of Ni into the subsurface region of Pt(111); the possibility of the production of the PtNiPt(111) structure, with Ni atoms staying directly underneath the surface Pt, was further suggested from the DFT modeling and experimental measurements of chemical properties, as described later.\"", "English": "The characterization of Ni/Pt bimetallic surfaces, synthesized by depositing a Ni monolayer on Pt(111) single crystal or polycrystalline Pt substrates, is conducted using a wide range of experimental techniques and DFT modeling. When Ni is deposited with the Pt(111) surface held at 300 K, Ni atoms stay on the topmost layer to produce the NiPt(111) surface MBS structure. If this surface is subsequently heated to 600 K, or if the monolayer deposition occurs with the Pt(111) substrate held at 600 K, most of the Ni atoms diffuse into the subsurface region to produce the PtNiPt(111) subsurface MBS structure. The surfaces are characterized using AES, XPS, LEIS, and STM. The LEIS and AES results following the annealing of the 300 K NiPt(111) surface to 900 K are shown in Fig. 5. The normal and grazing emission XPS of the NiPt(111) surface prepared at 300 K and the PtNiPt(111) subsurface structure prepared at 600 K are shown in Fig. 6. STM was also utilized to further characterize the morphology of the 300 K and 600 K surfaces. The AES, LEIS, XPS, and STM results confirmed the presence of a surface Ni monolayer on Pt(111) after the deposition of Ni at 300 K. The characterization following the annealing to 600640 K was consistent with the diffusion of Ni into the subsurface region of Pt(111); the possibility of the production of the PtNiPt(111) structure, with Ni atoms staying directly underneath the surface Pt, was further suggested from the DFT modeling and experimental measurements of chemical properties. This process is crucial for structural modeling, DFT calculations, and our comprehensive understanding of the electronic and chemical properties of these bimetallic surfaces in the context of advanced surface science and catalysis research.", "Chinese": "通过在300 K下将Ni沉积在Pt(111)表面上，Ni原子停留在最顶层，形成NiPt(111)表面MBS结构。如果随后将该表面加热至600 K，或者在600 K下将Pt(111)基板进行单层沉积，大多数Ni原子会扩散到Pt(111)的次表面区域，形成PtNiPt(111)次表面MBS结构。使用AES、XPS、LEIS和STM对Ni/Pt双金属表面进行表征。图5显示了将300 K NiPt(111)表面加热至900 K后的LEIS和AES结果。图6显示了在300 K下制备的NiPt(111)表面和在600 K下制备的PtNiPt(111)次表面结构的正常和掠射发射XPS。STM也被用来进一步表征300 K和600 K表面的形貌。AES、LEIS、XPS和STM结果证实，在300 K下沉积Ni后，Pt(111)表面存在一层Ni单层。在600640 K下退火后的表征与Ni扩散到Pt(111)的次表面区域一致；从DFT建模和化学性质的实验测量中进一步提出了PtNiPt(111)结构的可能性，其中Ni原子直接位于表面Pt下方。这一过程对于结构建模、DFT计算以及我们对这些双金属表面在高级表面科学和催化研究背景下的电子和化学性质的全面理解至关重要。", "Doi": "10.1016/j.surfrep.2008.02.001"},
{"Quotes": "[1] \"In many cases, these unique properties result in activities and/or selectivities that exceed those achievable with a monometallic catalyst. For this reason, there have been many fundamental experimental and theoretical studies of the novel properties of well-defined bimetallic surfaces [2] ,[3] ,[4] ,[5] ,[6] ,[7] ,[8] ,[9] .\"\n          [2] \"To study the modification effects on surface chemistry due to bimetallic formation, a monolayer film of one metal can be deposited onto a single-crystal substrate of another metal. Lattice mismatch results in the contraction or expansion of adlayer metalmetal bond length compared with that of the bulk metal, leading to a modification of the surface electronic properties due to the strain effect [6] ,[10] ,[11] .\"\n          [3] \"In addition, the formation of heterometallic bonds further alters the electronic properties of the surface, which is often referred to as the ligand effect.\"\n          [4] \"One useful parameter to describe the changes in the electronic properties of bimetallic surfaces is the position of the surface d-band center with respect to the Fermi level [12] .\"\n          [5] \"This parameter has been shown to strongly correlate with the ability of bimetallic surfaces to bind with small adsorbates, such as atomic hydrogen and oxygen [13] , alkenes [8] ,[14] , and oxygenates [15] ,[16] .\"\n          [6] \"In addition, activation barriers to such reactions as ethylene and maleic anhydride hydrogenation also have been correlated with the surface d-band center [8] ,[17] .\"\n          [7] \"Thus, its determination may enable first-principles predictions of bimetallic surfaces with desirable catalytic properties for reactions involving these molecules [18] .\"\n          [8] \"In the present work, a combination of density functional theory (DFT) modeling and surface science experiments was used to study the effects of bimetallic formation on the binding of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene, as well as on the low-temperature hydrogenation of cyclohexene.\"\n          [9] \"This was done by modifying Pt(111) with several 3d transition metals, including Fe, Co, Ni, and Cu.\"\n          [10] \"Depositing these metals on a Pt(111) single-crystal surface at room temperature was found to result in the formation of a surface monolayer of the 3d metals; these surfaces are designated as 3d-Pt-Pt(111).\"\n          [11] \"At elevated temperatures, the formation of a surface alloy is observed for each Pt-3d pair [9] ,[19] ,[20] ,[21] ,[22] ,[23] ,[24] ,[25] ,[26] ,[27] .\"\n          [12] \"These surface alloys have been shown to be enriched in Pt in the first atomic layer due to the enthalpic driving potential created by the lower surface energy of Pt compared with the 3d metals under consideration [28] ,[29] .\"\n          [13] \"Strain also may play a part in the interdiffusion of the Pt and 3d metals, because elastic strain is reduced by having the larger Pt atoms in the topmost atomic layer [23] .\"\n          [14] \"These Pt-enriched bimetallic surfaces are designated Pt-3d-Pt(111) in this study.\"\n          [15] \"Kitchin et al. [28] studied Ni modification of Pt(111) and found that surface Ni shifts the surface d-band center closer to the Fermi level in comparison to Ni(111), whereas subsurface Ni in the second atomic layer moves the d-band center away from the Fermi level.\"\n          [16] \"The current study extends these findings to Fe-, Co-, and Cu-modified Pt(111) surfaces.\"\n          [17] \"Cyclohexene can undergo decomposition, dehydrogenation, and self-hydrogenation (disproportionation) reactions, as well as hydrogenation in the presence of co-adsorbed atomic hydrogen.\"\n          [18] \"Due to the competitive nature of these reaction pathways, it is an ideal probe molecule for comparing the general trends in the chemical properties of the various bimetallic surfaces.\"\n          [19] \"On Pt(111), cyclohexene undergoes dehydrogenation and decomposition [7] ,[30] ; however, when Pt(111) is modified with another metal, the dominant reaction pathways can vary markedly.\"\n          [20] \"For example, modification with Sn can promote reversible adsorption, making molecular desorption the dominant pathway.\"\n          [21] \"Previous studies on 3d-modified Pt(111) have shown that the subsurface Pt-Ni-Pt(111) and Pt-Co-Pt(111) structures exhibit a novel low-temperature hydrogenation pathway [28] ,[31] ,[32] .\"\n          [22] \"Similar results were observed in the current study for the Pt-Fe-Pt(111) surface; however, the Pt-Cu-Pt(111) surface did not exhibit the same hydrogenation pathway.\"\n          [23] \"Furthermore, the current study also investigated the hydrogenation pathway on the four 3d-Pt-Pt(111) surfaces and found that this pathway did not occur on these surface structures because of the strong binding of cyclohexene and atomic hydrogen.\"\n          [24] \"The combined experimental results and DFT modeling allow us to establish a volcano-type relationship between the binding energies and hydrogenation activities among the various 3d/Pt(111) bimetallic surfaces.\"\n          [25] \"In the present work, a combination of density functional theory (DFT) modeling and surface science experiments was used to study the effects of bimetallic formation on the binding of atomic hydrogen and cyclohexene, as well as on the low-temperature hydrogenation of cyclohexene.
